< Review>
This is a very popular shop to get pizza in SLO, since they offer great deals on their very good pizzas. you wont get anything fancy from them, but thats what they are, they offer solid quality food at very affordable prices. Me and my friends get pizza delivered by them whenever we are in the mood for pizza since you can get 2 large pizzas for $14, which is a great deal for the quality. oh, and one of their most popular pizzas is their delicious chicken and white sauce, that is usually the one that disappears first when everyone gets at the food.

The employees are all very pleasant and they usually deliver in a more than acceptable time frame, so if you are craving pizza and you are in SLO, unless you want to get it at a sit-down restaurant, I would say the best choice is Fattes.</Review>

< review>
I am so confused by all the negative reviews. I walked in,and was kindly greeted by the owner almost immediately. He asked me if i wanted breakfast or lunch. I said breakfast, he recommended the breakfast sandwich on the Texas toast. IT IS ONE OF THE BEST BREAKFAST SANDWICHES IN THE EAST BAY. Yes, it's a bit greasy (like a good b-fast sandwich should be) but not too much to handle. I was blown away at the care he took in making it for me. The coffee was solid. The guy who runs this place really cares about his craft, don't know why all these people are hating. He makes juices from scratch in the mornings! Give this place a shot. It's really pretty good. It's not Farley's but it deserves to stick around.   And don't trust anyone reviewing bagels on the west coast - if they're not going to bagel shops for their bagels, then they don't know anything... Try the Texas toast! Dee Spot is doing something different in a nice way.< /review>

<Rating>5< /Rating>< text>
Josh & Chan make a great cappuccino! I go out of my way for it. Also, they just started baking their own GF bread in house - so awesome. Chan's a great guy & he goes out of his way to talk with (and listen to) his customers in order to understand our preferences.

*I was just chatting with Chan & discovered that they donate all excess pastries & other expired foods to the local community on a weekly basis!*

Bottom line is that Dee Spot is definitely putting their best foot forward to contributing to, and being a part of the local community.< /text>

< user_name>
Bill Say<//user_name>
<GmapID>0x8097baca1a07b5bb:0x3f5be54647e1a3d< /GmapID>< Review>
If hell served a beef taco

A lot of people like this place as evidenced by the crowd.  We did not. Now, call us foolish to not order burgers or ice cream at a clearly classic burger/soft serve ice cream joint and compound that with ordering tacos. That said, my fish tacos we're pretty ok and my wife's beef tacos were absolutely the worst either of us have ever had. First she said no onions and they loaded them on both her tacos and side salad. Next, the beef. Oh the beef. If ever the environmental movement needed a clear way to dissuade the world to stop eating beef this would have worked. Overnight cessation of beef eating. Guaranteed. Greasy like crazy and a taste like, hmmm...I think an Amazon box sauteed with Schillings Taco Seasoning would win in side by side taste comparisons. My father who grew up with dire food shortages in Korea drilled into us to eat every grain of rice on our plates, a rule I mostly still follow and respect. I fully supported my wife stopping at bite three or so. I tried one bite and out of sheer awe tried one more.  I did the honors of tossing them as Jolly Kone was already closed by this moment of post prandial trauma. I don't so lightly slam a business nor another's cooking though judging by the crowds and online reviews my petty feedback will not damage business. But if you value and respect to any degree the art form that is the beef taco, I highly recommend that you pass on Tasty Kone's version.< /Review>

< text>
These guys were great from the start! I called in to ask for a quick quote and discuss my issue, and they took the time to listen to me ramble and provide feedback on what they thought the issue was and the ballpark cost. The entire process was so easy and the communication was great with where my drone was in the process of being repaired (emails and texts once received, repaired, and shipped). I sent the drone in on a Thursday, received a very fair quote early the next day, then they got the drone back to me the following Tuesday. Very quick turn around, much better than I would have expected.
But this is where I was most impressed - when I opened the box the drone came back with a broken part that seemed to have been caused by how FedEx handled the package. I emailed Aerialpixels to let them know as soon as I discovered the issue (at about 9p.m.)...they responded almost immediately and with no questions asked they apologized and sent me a prepaid return label within 30 mins so they could fix the issue. I sent it back yesterday, they fixed it today, and its on it's way back to me overnight delivery. That is how you run a business!!!</text>

<rate>5< /rate><text>Best place in LA for drone repair and parts. Everyone is super helpful and professional, only going here from now on!<//text><pics>None</pics><Resp>None</Resp><gmapID>0x80c29c1482915231:0x9e5e44114f41912c</gmapID></record></dataset><record>
<review>To their credit, I commend Aerial Pixel for all the positive feedback they are receiving from their customers(only 2 negative). Obviously they are doing something right. I'm aware then, that I'm in the minority when saying  however, that my experience with them wasn't as pleasant.  It seems to me that most, if not all of the positive reviews come from people who's work was done right for them the first time. The problem seems to be when they misdiagnose a problem, such as in my case and also as in Mr. Dru Magtoto's case 5 months ago(one of the 2 negative reviews). The initial diagnosis of my Mavic Pro was for the replacement of the flat ribbon cable($200), which I paid.  When I picked it up, I asked the gentleman if everything were OK. He said he flew it for several minutes and everything looked good.  The first time I flew it up the "unstable gimbal" reading showed on the monitor. I wasn't sure if that was a normal reading, but also thought it may have been because it was windy that day. A couple days later, I decided to try it again and this time the same thing, except another reading which was unusual, plus the gimbal was spinning in different directions. I then called Aerial Pixel and clearly stated to the young lady on the phone that I was having some excessive readouts on my Mavic and I didn't think all of my issues were resolved during the repairs. I also mentioned that I couldn't bring it in right away,  but wanted to make sure that they'd have a record of the problem. She said to just bring it back and they'd take another look at it.  I took it back and several days later, I received their email and the diagnosis was "replace flat ribbon".....again! But this time, the estimate was $185. I called back and told them that they already replaced the flat ribbon. I talked to Joe and he said that it could be something else, which would cost more. I then said "forget it" and I'd come get it, but he then calmly, but firmly reminded me I'd still owe $75 for the second "diagnosis" since it was after 30 days. So that would be $275 for a problem that wasn't fixed? I'm thinking "what about my calling you guys before the 30 days?".  I then told him to go ahead and fix it. On the 3rd diagnosis, the estimate was $275 to replace the gimbal frame. I finally got it back and the total cost was $475.  I flew it today for the first time and still got "unstable gimbal" . I don't know, maybe it's a normal reading. I do know that even if it hasn't been totally fixed and I'm clearly within the new "30 day" time frame, I'm not taking it back. I feel that as a business, they should realize  that they will have some situations where they will have to give extra time and effort(such as in Mr Magtoto's and my case), but in doing so, they would keep those customers. Also, to their credit, they did warn me that I needed new propellers. Seemingly nice people though.<//review>< Name>

These guys are great!
My DJI Phantom 3 was not connecting to my RC after I accidentally left my drone powered on when I put it back in its storage case. The battery overheated and fried the receiver module in the drone.
Aerialpixels diagnosed the problem immediately and ordered a new receiver module.
From dropoff to pickup they kept me informed every step of the way with their online repair ticket system. I knew when my drone was being diagnosed, what parts had been ordered and what the price would be.
I didn't pay anything until my drone was 100% fixed and they tested it in front of me.
I am a busy pilot shooting real estate so every day without a drone is lost revenue, I appreciated their knowledge and efficiency...I was flying again less than an hour after I left their store and my repaired drone performed flawlessly!

< review>
Joe provided excellent service when I dropped my Phantom 4 and caused some gimbal damage. He helped me figure out a plan of action that met my needs with as low a cost as possible. He and his lead tech, Kavi, seem extremely knowledgeable about the DJI product line.

I have had a very strange descent problem with my quad that caused a crash from high altitude last year. I always assumed that it was my fault, but Joe spent extra time investigating the issue and he feels strongly that an equipment defect caused the problem because he has never seen as issue like it before. However, because resolving this issue was beyond the scope of services provided by AerialPixels, Joe suggested I contact DJI. Unfortunately, DJI wasn't willing to investigate the issue free of charge. Although my flight logs demonstrate that the issue started occurring during the warranty period, my quad still doesn't qualify for warranty service because I didn't report the issue until the warranty period expired. So, I have an otherwise healthy Phantom 4 with a bizarre descent issue that could come back to bite me sometime.< /review>

< review>
Popeyes Louisiana Kitchen, located in scenic and historical Covina California, features great tasting Louisiana style chicken and fresh made biscuits.
They have a wide variety of side dishes and a great selection of soft drinks and tea.
They have a drive through and inside, the restaurant is sparkling clean with plenty of seats and windows all around .Clean restrooms as well.
Popeyes Louisiana Kitchen in Covina California has a friendly staff and very helpful.
Family, kid and senior friendly,
It's a great eating experience !< /review>

< review>
I rarely eat at Popeye's and it appears I'll be eating there even less now. My debit card and credit cards got demagnetized earlier this week and the new ones haven't arrived yet. I waited for 15 minutes in the drive-thru to be told they don't have the ability to enter the number manually. I don't know if the corporate higher ups don't want minimum wage employees to take on big tasks like punching in the digits on the card or if the teens of today aren't capable but it's disgraceful! I don't think it's the latter as the young man who helped me seemed up for the challenge and more than capable but when he asked the manager how to enter the numbers, the voice bellowing across the kitchen said, "We can't enter the numbers." Technology can't help this problem. This is a Popeye's issue. On the positive side, my $86 order was wasted as it got made but not paid for. I'd fix this if I owned a Popeye's. It seems like wasting food when people are hungry and customers time while not taking in a penny because of something businesses have been handling seamlessly for decades is a joke but it's not! I'm dead serious. Popeye's can't take demagnetized cards even if they're chipped. Since I know this is a problem I'll likely waste more of my time and place several orders a day using my demagnetized card so Popeye's goes bankrupt while employees eat the wasted food for free.<//review>

< text>
Standard Cajun fast food and offering drive through and delivery during coronavirus. Note that it took 50 minutes of waiting in the drive through line to get our food; there was one smart person who left the line and parked to pick up food. They were able to do that and get their food prior to us placing our order.

They skimped on the Cajun fries, which was disappointing. That being said, I was glad to finally have been able to try the much hyped spicy chicken sandwich. The sandwich is much bigger than the equivalent chickfila sandwich, but the spiciness comes from the sauce rather than the chicken itself. I liked how the chicken was breaded and it was still crunchy even after the 20 minute car ride home. The sauce wasn‚Äôt spread evenly though, so I would suggest spreading it out yourself with a knife if you get takeout. The sandwich does come with pickles, and you can get a non-spicy sandwich (although the spicy sandwich is definitely manageable, and in the same level as hot Cheetos).<//text>

<Review>I really wanted to like this Popeye's as it is close to my house. The good news is that the food is delicious. It is my favorite takeout fried chicken and I really like their unique side dishes. The bad news is that while the people who help you are very nice, they don't seem to be very good at getting your order correct. My wife and I recently ordered the Tuesday special which is one leg and one thigh. We got three of them. When we got home, we found that we had one breast and one wing in all three orders. We wanted dark meat! On previous trips, we have ordered half mild and half spicy and received either all spicy or all mild. This last Tuesday, we went in to get the Tuesday special only to be told that they had temporarily stopped the Tuesday special because they keep running out of chicken. It's  Popeye's, they should never run out of chicken! It seems like poor management and poor training or maybe they just don't care. This is not rocket science! If you work at a chicken restaurant, you should be able to tell the difference between white and dark meat. I hope that they get their act together soon!
